< Text>
Currently attending their 7th anniversary. Full bar. I've been a semi regularly since the "new" grand opening about 7+ years ago. Anyhow, it's a cozy local bar, chill, friendly, affordable, with a great rotating indie beer selection (Stan's the man!). Good juke box. Amazing tacos (Taco Reyes is next door, as in, a shared wall next door) One Dart Board. Many photos. Lots of good times.</Text>

<review>Another reason to visit Paso Robles. We came for a wine country weekend and Sensorio for something to do in the evening. Only a couple of miles up 46 past 101.

They do do a temp check (as of 4-24-21) a bag check and there and you are responsible for social-distancing yourself on the walk. People can kind of crowd so it up to you to make space - and its dark.

Best time to come is just before sundown so you can get the contrast of the night sky above, dusk on the horizon and the lights.

We paid extra for the VIP but I don't think it was worth it personally. You have a place to sit above the walk and one free drink but the night we came it was soooo damn cold and the wind blowing we couldn't enjoy it.</review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipObyOlJ_VgplqdVulpvrDDBEs1RutCNSff0L-vs=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOD8_vUvC0yNU2ry_BOZaoPky9c4-u4d9SNyj2g=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics><Resp>None< /Resp>< gmapID>

<rate>5<//rate>< review>
We had a nice night. Arrived before sunset, grabbed an 805 beer & some food at the food truck court before enjoying a friday evening stroll around the grounds. I do think that eventually, post Covid-19, the light towers would be an awesome area ro add synchronized music & dancing; maybe as part of the VIP passes. As a photographer ot would be cool to have this used as a midnight astrophotography workshop venue where someone could pay a fair amount of money to receive professional instruction & use a tripod. The possibilities for this venue are endless so if you've already been I think they will be able to continue to entice return engagement of new exhibits & changes. Maybe even future concert grounds. Who knows, but as a local I did find this a nice evening for local & tourists alike . . .</review>

I know it's called "field of lights" but it was honestly a little underwhelming we we arrived and realized it was literally just a field full of fiber optic lights with globes on top. It felt overpriced for the overall experience. Definitely don't buy VIP tickets, I could not see anything appealing about the VIP terrace. < text>
We got the VIP tix and they were well worth it. We went when they opened (in order to watch the transformation from light to sunset) and we bypassed the already very very long line and were escorted to a roped off area with heaters, fireplaces and tables and chairs and an airstream ‚Äúbar‚Äù where one could order beer wine and champagne. Very nice experience. We had our wine and then decided to walk the path of which there are two. The longer path is not at all long so o would recommend that path. It‚Äôs a very easy walk. There are about 5-6 food trucks and various benches around the area. But seating is limited for the non-VIP ticket holders FYI< /text>

< Text>
Amazing art installation! Truly huge, covers acres of rolling hills with fiber optic lights that change colors. Food and drinks (including local beer and wine) are available Spectacular, highly recommended. It can be cold at night so bring a sweater or coat.</Text>

Color, outdoors, live music and just sitting and watching. Sounds simple and usual, but the colors change all evening the outdoor venue is dark but strolling or sitting and watching is a comfortable pace. Live music is in the background and too bad because it's usually quite nice. Sitting and watching is ever so good in these busy times.< /text>

<Name>Kimberly Ann Graham<//Name><time>1568298507301</time><Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
Breathtaking! I highly recommend coming out while this installation is here. I also would recommend that you get a time slot that starts before the sun sets so that you can enjoy seeing the field during the process of the sun coming down and the lights coming up! There is plenty of parking and they limit entries to 75 people part time slot. I imagine it could get crowded but it certainly wasn't on my visit. As for accessibility, this has been designed with that in mind. All of the trails are 100% wheelchair accessible. They also have a large golf cart shuttle that will bring you from the parking area to the start of the trail around the field.  for food, the menu is a bit pedestrian so I can't recommend getting food here but the wine list is far better than average. The Opollo Zinfandel was delightful and served in a plastic stemless glass so it could be taken out on the trail.  No selfie sticks or tripods allowed but photography is welcome as long as it is personal photos & video.  they have blankets to rent for $5 if you fail to dress properly for the evening. They also have games on the lawn and a picnic area for food purchased on site. No outside food or beverages allowed.<//text>

<GmapID>0x80ecc5443242f2c1:0xbf8e837bf16cd744<//GmapID><name>Shirley Gerardy< /name>< Review>
The light display is lovely.  We really enjoyed photographing the colorful hillsides as we meandered through the lights. We selected the second hour so we could have dinner beforehand.  There may be photo ops at the first hour when the sky is not quite as dark.  Our disappointment was that the one-way path is not clearly marked. There are arrows on the ground which are difficult or impossible to see and little to no signage or human direction, except when you have already gone the wrong way.  There were also dark areas where the lights were out.  Don't recommend until these issues are fixed.</Review>

<userid>104283237201242085973<//userid>< Name>
Bondiamo<//Name>
< Time>
1573096857044</Time>
<rate>4< /rate>< Text>
Unique experience that's literally a field of lights. We arrived before sundown to see what the installation looked like before dark. You can choose the VIP experience which included a boxed dinner, two drinks, and a reserved seating patio or join the commoners like us grabbing a glass of wine and some tacos from Ricky‚Äôs Mexican food truck permanently parked on site. We walked through the paths woven between a few large Oaks to view the open areas filled with small spheres that would soon be illuminated by fiber-optic light, gently swaying on their long stems. Very cool as the dusk turns to night, the moon hangs overhead filtering between the outstretched Oak branches while the thousands of small spheres gently change color. Not something we thought would be captivating but certainly was a sight to see. The installation is currently scheduled to run until January 2020, followed by grand plans for a new Hotel, Resort, and Botanical garden.< /Text>

<review>Such an amazing experience! $30 (if you pay online), $34 + change (if you buy tickets from the gate). The employees are great, the bathroom is clean and modern, and nice music. As you pass the "activity center", you'll see the field of lights. The walk path is a little bit too dark (hope they add some very dim lights). I was awe by how majestic this place is! You can't do flash photography unfortunately, and you cannot use tripod too (you gotta be creative for manual exposure) . If you are planning to go take a photo of yourself with the background, use another phone and turn up its brightness and get a white background so you can use it as your mini spotlight!! Overall, I'm really happy with the experience that I have. It does feel like I'm on a magical place. I do hope someday this place gets improved over time. If Holidays are coming, I hope they put lights on the trees as well. Put more lights around the  area (even in the parking lot). I also hope they add more grass area there (fake or not). I would suggest you to wear shoes as the trail is sandy.  Overall, I HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS PLACE!

Update: I highly recommend you use a phone with night mode- such as Galaxy S10, Note 10 and iPhone 11 Pro< /review>< Resp>

< Review>
It is something you should try to see at least once. One thing was that the pizza booth worker was flustered or just off but he got our order wrong then didn't want us to pay until we were going to leave, we tried multiple times & we'd get sent away. At first it wasn't a big deal we assumed he didn't want to get his hands dirty cause he was in the middle of making multiple pizzas. Then we go a third time & he stares blankly, we asked if he took card before ordering & we reminded him of this, but he didn't have his phone or card reader it was a bit odd. Anyways ! The tickets do run quite high especially cause there is not too many food options or alcohol, so that is why this will be a one time thing. The art is solar powered & the lights don't turn on until the sun is down, so if you do get the 7pm ticket you may have to wait until 8pm or so to actually see them lit up. But it is absolutely amazing to get there early & see how everything looks before the lights come on & then as each one slowly comes on. It is breathtaking & at some time you should put your phone down & just enjoy the view.</Review>

<time>1561267133044</time>< Review>
This is an...interesting experience. This is a set of 50k+ fiber optic cables that are fed into frosted plastic bulbs roughly 2" in diameter,  that look like the dandelions ready to seed that you blow. They are spread across a small valley and very (very) slowly change colors. No music, just walk through them. To give one credit, it's peaceful. Everyone was uniformly looking for spots as if something was going to happen...nope.

On the other hand, for the price it's expensive unless if you REALLY care about your Instagram. It's a 20 minute walk through high tech Christmas lights in a field for almost $40. This is a $20 experience, tops.

If this wasn't enough, we bought tickets for 8:30 pm, our tickets said that "your wave starts at 8". We show up at 8 and then are told they don't even start processing the line until 8:30. It's 9 and we finally made it in.

Supposedly it's between this and a botanical garden. City officials: pick the botanical garden.< /Review>

< Rating>
5</Rating>
<Review>I loved it! Its worth the $$ and drive if you're coming from a distance. We went within the first couple weeks of opening so things may change as time goes on.
-Waze had us turn into the wrong street which had us making a few u-turns on the freeway to get to the entrance.
-We chose the first time slot so we had plenty of time to eat and enjoy the live music before the sunset. You'll be fine with any time slot you choose.
-Dont be afraid to wander thru the exhibit before the sun goes down. It'll be beautiful from anywhere you stand.
-You'll want to stay until closing so plan on staying in town for the night or prepare for a late drive home.
-The food available from the food truck is pretty tasty. The portions are enough to get you by but if you're looking to have a full meal, eat before.
-Bring a sweater, wear comfy shoes, leave the hydroflask in the car.
-I'm sure the VIP section is great, but there's nothing like hanging around with the commoners.
-The bathroom portable was clean and well stocked.
-I will most definitely be returning.< /Review>< Pics>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOUcSCjEDSD0ZO_eV2S5wCUF3eQf-n-Heog-x-V=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMGVEzQfzWGL-ga2p9uc4B4S354-nybg8eW6NXY=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNyslN4NqtoGQAHk6CsCxn-_ryXPuQsXCYdVEwq=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN2zmyrWVoI6Y8ZQ95dox4zLL9XA0FA5XD29odq=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMLyO1L-vVd2ob8M7c8skTJCcvSs5mZQXOpCxpC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>

This is a must see!!! It was recommended to us and now we are telling all out friends.

Not only do you get to see these neat lights, but you can see a beautiful sunset too!

It is a self guided, paved path to walk through the lights.

If you can't do the walk around, it is still a spectacular thing to see from one of the seated areas on top of the hill looking down onto the display.< /review>

< Review>
Sensorio is currently exhibiting Bruno Munro‚Äôs Field of Lights which is a solar powered art installation that spread through multiple acres of land. The field is lit by sphere pods connecting to fiber-optics. They change colors every few seconds. It‚Äôs a beautiful experience and photo op! Tickets are purchased online with designated time and date.

Entrance/Parking: The entrance is located on one side of the freeway so you might be routed to loop around. There is a right turn lane from the freeway that leads directly to the parking lot. They offer complementary parking and shuttle service. A 5 minute walk to the entrance.

I came during Memorial weekend and they‚Äôve been open for about a week now. It looks like they are not completely done with the construction for the event such as fence, pavement, and lights for the entrance but the art installation is ready to view.

At the entrance, I was told we couldn‚Äôt bring in any camera with detachable lenses because they consider those professional cameras... I wasn‚Äôt gonna let that go since we drove all the way and obviously want to take photos. So I went to talk to a few staff members and sadly they didn‚Äôt even know the difference between a prof. camera.... Luckily, the executive director was right next to me and she was able to clear the misunderstanding to her staff. CAMERAS ARE ALLOWED but no tripods, professional camera crews, & photos for commercial use. I felt bad for all the people that got turned away because they didn‚Äôt ask the right person.

They should‚Äôve also told everyone that The Field of Light doesn‚Äôt turn on until sunset. You can go in anytime after your ticket time until they close. It gets really windy at night, so definitely dress warm and consider scarfs and gloves!

Food/drinks: They currently have one food truck that serves light meals like hot dogs, pizza, hummus, & salad. Price ranging from $7-10. I‚Äôd recommend eating before you get there since there isn‚Äôt much food options in the area. The alcohol station offers beer and wine. We got a bottle of the red blend which was a better deal for 5 people for $38 vs $10 per glass. It had a sweet smokey taste, not bad.

Overall it‚Äôs worth a visit but they are probably still working out the details!< /Review>

This installation looks far better in pictures and in person and that is a tragedy. To those whom enjoy it, mazeltov but a single nights dive in a bioluminescent sea puts this display to shame and you can interact with it.  This feels like a pale, artificial impostor by comparison.< /Review>

(Translated by Google) Although he is in a remote location and takes time to arrive, but because of this, there will not be too many tourists in the venue, you will have enough time to appreciate, it is a beautiful experience, it is worth visiting.

The sea of ‚Äã‚Äãlights is very romantic, and the stars in the night sky are also beautiful.

< text>
They have a very wide selection of rough and polished stones, trinkets, and handmade jewelry and crafts, all at surprisingly low prices. It's a little hard to find, as it is tucked away in the back of the small plaza, but I would say it is well worth the trip. They even offer free little cards detailing all of the stone types with your purchase. This will be my first choice if I'm ever in the market to buy polished stones again.< /text>

< pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNANV4BPBotpS5oODABX0nenaNCyO3LIa1hevOY=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>
< review>
I was a little underwhelmed with cafe ficelle.

The overall menu looked interesting. And the food presentation was good. However, the taste of the food was mediocre at best.

We ordered the avocado toast. It looked delicious. The toast can only he described as tooth-breaker crunchy. It had a red spread which tasted very similar to a shrimp cocktail sauce and over-powered the avocado.

We also ordered the coque madame (pictured). It also looked very nice. It was better than the aforementioned toast. Egg, ham and cheese on bread.

Both plates came with a fruit salad. It was topped with some berries, but the bottom 3/4ths of the fruit cup was honeydew and cantaloupe.

The banana and nutella crepe was good... something worth returning for. The bananas were coated with sugar and gently flambayed.

Finally, price for iced tea was high enough to warrant a free refill, but they dont offer free refills. Had to settle for the offered iced tap water.<//review>

< review>
The entire marketplace is wonderful but the attached bakery has the best pastries in town; even better than the Amandine in Westwood (and that's saying something!). In fruit tarts, there's no comparison; they have multiple styles and shapes and they are never soggy... How do they do that? Try the Kievsky pastry--my gosh. I didn't think I could love Napoleans this much. So much delicious. No matter how much you buy, I can almost guarantee you will regret not buying more. Highly recommend.<//review>

Oh but the food makes up for the lack of amenities or style. It is literally like going to Grandma's house where she cooks for the family. I got 2 meals out of my entree. It was cooked fresh (you can look in the kitchen & watch her prepare your meal).

I will return!< /Review></record>

< Text>
This was a pretty weird dining experience. The one old man in the place seemed completely disinterested that I was there. I had to go through the kitchen and find him for a menu. He didn't speak English so I couldn't ask any questions about the choices so I Googled what was there. I was not offered any kind of beverage. After a good while, he came back with a plate of khinkalis which were pretty damn good. I had to go looking for him again to pay my bill. I think the food could make up for the spartan "decor" and complete lack of service, but just a little bit more would go a long way. Now that I know what to expect, I'll be a little more prepared next time.< /Text>
